    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

  <span id="freeText17901541503393634016" style="display:none"><b>Beyond the Martial Empire and within it, the threat of war looms ever larger.</b><br /><br />Helene Aquilla, the Blood Shrike, is desperate to protect her sister's life and the lives of everyone in the Empire. Yet danger lurks on all sides. Emperor Marcus, haunted by his past, grows increasingly unstable and violent, while Keris Veturia, the ruthless Commandant, capitalizes on the Emperor's volatility to grow her own power—regardless of the carnage she leaves in her path.<br /><br />Far to the east, Laia of Serra knows that the fate of the world lies not in the machinations of the Martial court, but in stopping the Nightbringer. During the hunt to bring him down, Laia faces unexpected threats from those she hoped would help her, and is drawn into a battle she never thought she'd have to fight.<br /><br />And in the land between the living and the dead, Elias Veturius has given up his freedom to serve as Soul Catcher. However, in doing so, he has vowed himself to an ancient power that demands his complete surrender—even if that means abandoning the woman he loves.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1745524050?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1745524050" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1123967218327618802"><blockquote>
  <i>“There are worse things than death,” I say. “Shall we learn about them together?”</i>
</blockquote><br/>4 1/2 stars. When it comes to heart-racing action scenes, I cannot think of another YA author who does it better than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7770873.Sabaa_Tahir' title='Sabaa Tahir' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sabaa Tahir</a>. She plunges you into the chaos almost immediately and once again, for the third book in a row, she keeps the drama and bloodshed coming until the very end.<br/><br/>The ONLY reason I rated this book slightly lower than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33602773.An_Ember_in_the_Ashes__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___1_' title='An Ember in the Ashes (An Ember in the Ashes, #1) by Sabaa Tahir' rel='nofollow noopener'>An Ember in the Ashes</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25558608.A_Torch_Against_the_Night__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___2_' title='A Torch Against the Night (An Ember in the Ashes, #2) by Sabaa Tahir' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Torch Against the Night</a> is that I felt like Eli</span>
  <span id="freeText1123967218327618802" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“There are worse things than death,” I say. “Shall we learn about them together?”</i>
</blockquote><br />4 1/2 stars. When it comes to heart-racing action scenes, I cannot think of another YA author who does it better than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7770873.Sabaa_Tahir" title="Sabaa Tahir" rel="nofollow noopener">Sabaa Tahir</a>. She plunges you into the chaos almost immediately and once again, for the third book in a row, she keeps the drama and bloodshed coming until the very end.<br /><br />The ONLY reason I rated this book slightly lower than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33602773.An_Ember_in_the_Ashes__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___1_" title="An Ember in the Ashes (An Ember in the Ashes, #1) by Sabaa Tahir" rel="nofollow noopener">An Ember in the Ashes</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25558608.A_Torch_Against_the_Night__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___2_" title="A Torch Against the Night (An Ember in the Ashes, #2) by Sabaa Tahir" rel="nofollow noopener">A Torch Against the Night</a> is that I felt like Elias's perspective didn't contribute as much to this installment until close to the end, and some of his chapters felt like superfluous filler. But maybe it was that Laia's and Helene's (sorry, the <i>Blood Shrike's</i>) perspectives were just so damn good that Elias's ghostly wanderings paled in comparison.<br /><br />If you've been enjoying this series up until now, there's no reason why your love shouldn't continue on with this book. The <b>stakes keep getting higher and the war keeps getting bigger</b>, leading to the kind of dramatic climax we would expect from this series. The body count is high, the reveals are exciting, and I am even more desperate for the next book than I was for this one.<br /><br />Just when you think things can't possibly get any worse in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30809786.A_Reaper_at_the_Gates__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___3_" title="A Reaper at the Gates (An Ember in the Ashes, #3) by Sabaa Tahir" rel="nofollow noopener">A Reaper at the Gates</a>, the delightfully evil Ms Tahir chuckles maniacally at her keyboard and - you guessed it - things get a whole lot worse.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>I will sing you such a story—a story that was long untold. The story of a name and its meaning. Of how that name matters more than any other single word in existence. But I must prepare myself, for such stories are dragons drawn from a deep well in a dark place. Does one summon a dragon? No. One may only invite it and hope it emerges.</i>
</blockquote><br />I'm not going to say too much about the story in case those reading this review haven't checked out the first two books yet. But I will say I like how the author created some more depth in a couple of the villainous characters in this book, turning them into fully-fleshed out human beings who are not just mindlessly evil (though they are still despicable). I also find the Nightbringer very interesting and I can't wait to read more about him.<br /><br />Overall, it's a bloody, nasty book in a bloody, nasty series. It's filled with prophecy, creepy ghosts, and jinn seeking vengeance. There's romance, but not that much. And it seems to promise some very dark and terrible things to come. I can't wait!<br /><br /><a href="http://emilymay.me/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1123967218327618802" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2450187703" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2450187703" />
    <a title="Warda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30036082-warda"><img alt="Warda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593385153p2/30036082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2450187703?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Warda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Warda" href="/user/show/30036082-warda">Warda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780008288754" href="/book/show/37901428-a-reaper-at-the-gates">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2450187703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16177421429581796204">Well, it seems like I’m in the major minority here. <br/>Three books in and I’m still not attached to the characters. If any of them had died in this book, I would’ve shrugged it off. <br/>Am I to blame? I don’t think so, since there barely was any backstory or development given to those characters. <br/><br/>Constant action, non-stop movement and not enough focus on our main characters. I had no option but to not form any attachment, since we weren’t given any breathing room for the plot to slow down and for it to</span>
  <span id="freeText16177421429581796204" style="display:none">Well, it seems like I’m in the major minority here. <br />Three books in and I’m still not attached to the characters. If any of them had died in this book, I would’ve shrugged it off. <br />Am I to blame? I don’t think so, since there barely was any backstory or development given to those characters. <br /><br />Constant action, non-stop movement and not enough focus on our main characters. I had no option but to not form any attachment, since we weren’t given any breathing room for the plot to slow down and for it to shift to the characters.<br /><br /><b>Book One</b> was great. It was gloriously fast paced and exciting and the plot kept me on the edge of my bed. I was on a high whilst reading it. <br /><br /><b>Book Two</b> was where I was expecting some kind of development to come in to play. But yet again, I feel like we weren’t given any and the focus was still on the plot and these characters trying to navigate and fix the messed up world they lived in. <br /><br />I made up excuses and thought, you know what? They’re on the run, these kids are at war, there just isn’t enough time for their history to be explored in detail, because it’s unrealistic to expect that. It’s war after all. Surely, Book Three will touch upon something though. <br /><br />And it did. <i>‘A Reaper at the Gates’</i> gave me glimpses of backstory and history to SOME of the characters (which was BEAUTIFUL!) and how they ended up where they are now. Just a small glimpse into a FEW of them, before the plot took centre stage again. <br /><br />At this point I couldn’t think of anymore excuses to give and just became fuckin’ annoyed that these characters had no substance and weren’t convincing in their power and magic at all. <br /><br />HOW do you ignore Darin? WHY on fucks earth wasn’t he given any kind of focus after what he went through? Laia and her abilities weren’t expanded upon. She just has them apparently. And is a leader now. HOW? Her whole tone is so insecure. Helene is just shouting out orders and isn’t achieving anything with it or learning from her mistakes. And Elias and his new role. We weren’t walked through their magic, their training, their powers, and their fuckin’ abilities. <br /><br />We’ve had plenty of the ‘now moments’ thrown in. But still, there were no layers to these characters that ultimately led to their root and shaped them as a person. <br /><br />It was almost like <b>‘The Cruel Prince’</b> situation where everything was just more or less thrown at you and readers were expected to go with the flow, understand the world, the magic they possessed and form a bond though nothing substantial was provided. There was no form of structure to it all. Just random and it read messy to me. <br /><br />I’m angry. And so bitter. Am I the only one that doesn’t see it? Because please, if there was character development and I have missed out on it somehow, I happily welcome you to point out my stupidity.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16177421429581796204" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2331644642" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2331644642" />
    <a title="Renée Ahdieh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5021803-ren-e-ahdieh"><img alt="Renée Ahdieh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487663207p2/5021803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2331644642?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Renée Ahdieh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Renée Ahdieh" href="/user/show/5021803-ren-e-ahdieh">Renée Ahdieh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2331644642" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15596374131780136483">whyyyyy, sabaa, whyyyyyyy???<br/><br/>(aside: mwahahahahahaha)<br/><br/>you know how they tell you that good things come to those who wait? i never bought into this school of thought bc i'm pretty much veruca salt when it comes to books. but, holy hell, is A REAPER AT THE GATES worth it. i was immediately drawn back into this darkly dangerous world and all its amazing characters. each POV is distinct and painstakingly wrought. the action is intense, and the angst made my heart hurt for days afterward. it's smart, s</span>
  <span id="freeText15596374131780136483" style="display:none">whyyyyy, sabaa, whyyyyyyy???<br /><br />(aside: mwahahahahahaha)<br /><br />you know how they tell you that good things come to those who wait? i never bought into this school of thought bc i'm pretty much veruca salt when it comes to books. but, holy hell, is A REAPER AT THE GATES worth it. i was immediately drawn back into this darkly dangerous world and all its amazing characters. each POV is distinct and painstakingly wrought. the action is intense, and the angst made my heart hurt for days afterward. it's smart, sexy, and gut-wrenching. exactly what you've come to expect from the brilliance of sabaa tahir.<br /><br />all i'm saying is that i need more. now. in veruca salt singing voice: DON'T CARE HOW, I WANT IT NOWWWWWWW.<br /><br /> </span>

<div id="review_2605441484" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2605441484" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2605441484?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780008288754" href="/book/show/37901428-a-reaper-at-the-gates">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2605441484" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8613480410968897746">it is with a heavy heart and sorrowful soul that i have to rate this book anything lower than 5 stars (i actually may change and round up because a 3 feels sooo harsh at the moment), because this series has been absolutely stellar up until this point. <br/><br/>i get that a story is meant to have opposition. a character grows and develops through it and because of it. without opposition, there would be no resolution. but i also feel that it is important for a character to have hope and to have success alo</span>
  <span id="freeText8613480410968897746" style="display:none">it is with a heavy heart and sorrowful soul that i have to rate this book anything lower than 5 stars (i actually may change and round up because a 3 feels sooo harsh at the moment), because this series has been absolutely stellar up until this point. <br /><br />i get that a story is meant to have opposition. a character grows and develops through it and because of it. without opposition, there would be no resolution. but i also feel that it is important for a character to have hope and to have success along the way, some light at the end of tunnel to encourage a reader to continue reading and become invested. so when multiple characters are constantly struggling and failing at every turn, for nearly 500 pages, it gets sooo discouraging and annoying. not one single thing goes right in this story, causing to me to forever associate this book with the massive amounts of frustration and negativity i felt whilst reading this. which is never something you want with a book. <br /><br />and because of that, this book only further confirms the nagging suspicions created by the second book that this story is going in a direction that i do not like, nor signed up for.<i>‘an ember in the ashes’</i> is such an outstanding book, but this story feels sooo far from that little gem of brilliance and i am deeply saddened by that. <br /><br />the writing is still top quality, the plot is action-packed and fast paced, and the characters are intriguing. so i have no doubts as to why so many love this book, but i personally cant get past the lack of hope and constant presence of frustration in this story. i will read the final book when its released because i have made it this far, but i very much doubt the conclusion will be as amazing as its beginning. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8613480410968897746" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2092645939" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2092645939" />
    <a title="alana ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12402009-alana"><img alt="alana ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599221603p2/12402009.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2092645939?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="alana ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="alana ♡" href="/user/show/12402009-alana">alana ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12402009-alana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2092645939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3144651735584860490">It’s amazing how we willingly pay to be traumatized,  but honestly I’d do it all over again if I could. I have to say, there is no one in the writing game quite like Sabaa Tahir when it comes to opening up <strong>EVERY</strong> book with heart-pounding intensity. With that being said I was already terrified to start this book knowing that and also because, let's face it, Sabaa is also not the kindest to her characters. When I read the first 80 pages of this book I <strong>NOPED</strong> and put it down so fast not because it wa</span>
  <span id="freeText3144651735584860490" style="display:none">It’s amazing how we willingly pay to be traumatized,  but honestly I’d do it all over again if I could. I have to say, there is no one in the writing game quite like Sabaa Tahir when it comes to opening up <strong>EVERY</strong> book with heart-pounding intensity. With that being said I was already terrified to start this book knowing that and also because, let's face it, Sabaa is also not the kindest to her characters. When I read the first 80 pages of this book I <strong>NOPED</strong> and put it down so fast not because it wasn't good, but because things were not going well for the characters and I knew it was about to get <strong>SO MUCH WORSE</strong>. <br /><br />Spoiler alert: it did.<br /><br />After almost a month of a hiatus from this I decided I just needed to rip the bandaid off and get it over with. So despite knowing that my heart was about to get stomped on I willingly dove myself back into the story of Laia, Elias, and Helene for the third time and I was not disappointed. Heartbroken and absolutely terrified for book four? <strong>YES.</strong> Disappointed? Never. I honestly don't think there is a word that can accurately describe how afraid I am for book four. I think after this book I may actually like Laia a little bit more. If you know me you know she and I never really connected and forget about me shipping her with Elias. It'll never happen. But nonetheless, I did find myself feeling something slightly other than nothing for Laia. Helene, on the other hand, oh how my heart bleeds for her. Some things will never change. She is my queen.<br /><br />Anyway, I really struggle with writing reviews multiple books into a series because just about everything is a spoiler, so I'm going to keep this as simple and as vague as possible. Laia, Helene, and Elias are all doing their own thing. The Commandant is still being a selfish bitch. War is coming. People are dying left and right. Hearts are breaking. Necks are snapping. War is now here. The Nightbringer is trying to wreak havoc on the world. <strong>NOTHING IS OKAY. </strong>Yep, that's basically a summary of the book.<br /><br /><b>Three things I loved most about this book are:</b><br /><br />1.Finding out Cook's backstory, if you know you're probably sobbing with me<br />2.Helene and Harper's slow burn romance?!?! <strong>SOMEONE PLEASE TELL ME YOU FEEL THE SAME WAY<br /></strong>3. The wild ending battle absolutely annihilated my hopes that this will have a happy ending but ya girl is still trying to gather the pieces of my shattered hopes and dreams. They might be slipping through my fingers, but I'll never give up on these characters, especially my queen.<br /><br /><b>Favorite Quotes</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"Pain is a choice. Succumb to it and fail. Or defy it and Triumph.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“Strange how monsters can reach from beyond the grave, as potent in death as they were in life.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><blockquote>
  <em>"Mercy, Blood Shrike. That is my order. I do not deserve it. I do not even wish it. But you'll give it to me anyway. Because you're good."</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />All in all, this book will take your heart on a treacherous journey of emotions and you will never be the same. But you still need this book in your life. If you haven't started this series I would <strong>HIGHLY</strong> recommend it and if you have started this series just know I'm sorry and you'll probably need a large dose of therapy by the time it's over!<br /><br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishchicksblog.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookishchick" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishchick_/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3144651735584860490" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer351717639036271059"><u>5 Sweet bleeding skies STAR'S</u> <br/><br/><i>“The sword point is my priest. The dance of death is my prayer. The killing blow is my release.”</i><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1531467086ra/25967466.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>“Hope is stronger than fear. It is stronger than hate.”</i><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453250960i/17803481._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/> <br/>Holly Mother!!! I don't even know what to say right now! I am completely speechless. 'A Reaper at the Gates' is utterly freaking brilliant! <b>BRILLIANT!</b> I was awestruck from beginning to end and I sure as hell didn't want to put it down. It's hypnotizing, once the pages started turning I couldn't stop. I have so many e</span>
  <span id="freeText351717639036271059" style="display:none"><u>5 Sweet bleeding skies STAR'S</u> <br><br><i>“The sword point is my priest. The dance of death is my prayer. The killing blow is my release.”</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1531467086ra/25967466.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>“Hope is stronger than fear. It is stronger than hate.”</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453250960i/17803481._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>Holly Mother!!! I don't even know what to say right now! I am completely speechless. 'A Reaper at the Gates' is utterly freaking brilliant! <b>BRILLIANT!</b> I was awestruck from beginning to end and I sure as hell didn't want to put it down. It's hypnotizing, once the pages started turning I couldn't stop. I have so many emotions swirling around right now. <i>Sabaa Tahir</i> has this way with her writing that makes the reader <b>FEEL</b> every emotion. The anger, the fear, the courage, the heartache and of course the love. And this has <b>ALL</b> the <b>FEELS</b>!!! It just pours into you and takes you on one hell of a journey. This book will NOT disappoint, it's very dark, dangerous and heart-stopping. From the writing to the plot, to the world-building all the way to the characters, everything is so captivating and completely addictive. I love the alternating POV's, they all connect together like a perfect puzzle piece. The character growth is confounding, with each new book, you discover whole new layers of who they are. I have grown deep attachments to these characters, even the bastards you wish death upon and when you finally get your wish you <i>mourn their loss</i> all the same. Not many authors can pull such a trick out of there hats. Everything was so well-paced and the battle scenes were devastating and thrilling all at once. This series is powerful and I never want it to end. <i>A Reaper at the Gates</i> ripped my heart wide open and made me cry and cry 😭😭! Oh, my poor beautiful Elias. I will not lose hope, for you are the most amazing of them all! Also, we discover Laia's mothers true identity and it's all just so damn sad! Laia and Helene are badass heroines and I can only imagine the unstoppable force they will be, being on the same side, for once. My excitement is bubbling over at the prospect 😁! I'm elated that we finally got to see more of the connection between Helene and Harper♥, now if Helene would get out of her own way :( Also, I love the character of Darin, Laia's brother and of course lets not forget the newcomer Musa. I really like him a lot and can't wait to know him more. I'm dying just thinking of the long wait I have ahead of me before I can read the next masterpiece in this series! <br><br><b>*Another stunning cover :D and that title couldn't be more perfect!*</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525979309i/25519070._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>“You are cruel, Elias,” she whispers against my mouth. <br>“To give a girl all she desires only to tear it away.”<br>“This isn't the end for us, Laia of Serra.” I cannot give up what we could have. <br>I don't care what bleeding vow I made. “Do you hear me? This is not our end.”<br>“You've never been a liar.” She dashes her hands against the wetness in her eyes. <br>“Don't start now.”</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1531467086ra/25967467.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>“What I feel for Elias is different, a flame I hold close to my heart when I feel my strength flagging. Sometimes, deep in the night as I travel, I picture a future with him. But I dare not look at too closely. How can I, When it can never be?”</i></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1807913615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9230915374381985337">im trying to imagine how it would feel to finish a book and NOT BE WORRIED ABOUT THE FATE OF MY BABIES IN THE FINAL BOOK<br/><br/>👏LET👏ELIAS👏AND👏LAIA👏BE👏HAPPY👏ᵖˡᵉᵃˢᵉ<br/><br/>4.5 stars<br/><br/><b>
  <i>buddy read</i>
</b> with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/57602032' rel='nofollow noopener'>this reading <s>disaster</s> machine</a><br/><br/>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br/><br/>what the heck happened to the matching cover designs????<br/><br/>the title is 💯💯💯👌👌👌💯💯 but the cover is so OFF AND NOW IM SAD AND CONFUSED WHY DONT WE HAVE MATCHING COVERS!!!!<br/><br/>. . . also. . .is anyone gonna mention how gorgeous elias looks??!?!?!!</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1706227888" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1706227888?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=why-yes-i-ya">why-yes-i-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=thanks-for-prezzies">thanks-for-prezzies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1706227888" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1532730882204007135"><b>oooh, goodreads choice awards semifinalist for best young adult fantasy 2018! what will happen?</b><br/><br/>this book is an inch-and-a-half thick and i was bored and shocked by my boredom until maybe the last quarter-inch. <br/><br/>i’d been looking forward to reading this <i>tremendously</i>, and when i finally carved out the space to get to it, i dove in like a fox in the snow<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533224431ra/26067061.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>but my elation was dampened by the slog of it, and i got sadder and sadder as the book refused to be as awesome as the first two. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533228024ra/26067250.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>it’s very convolute</span>
  <span id="freeText1532730882204007135" style="display:none"><b>oooh, goodreads choice awards semifinalist for best young adult fantasy 2018! what will happen?</b><br><br>this book is an inch-and-a-half thick and i was bored and shocked by my boredom until maybe the last quarter-inch. <br><br>i’d been looking forward to reading this <i>tremendously</i>, and when i finally carved out the space to get to it, i dove in like a fox in the snow<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533224431ra/26067061.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>but my elation was dampened by the slog of it, and i got sadder and sadder as the book refused to be as awesome as the first two. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533228024ra/26067250.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>it’s very convoluted and full of all that capital-letter shit that YA series overdo: <br><br><i>The Martials wield their weapons of war with merciless efficiency. They want to break the Scholars. And if I don’t stop the Nightbringer - if I don’t find this “Beekeeper” in Adisa - they will.</i> <br><br>&amp;etc. <br><br>also, i don’t personally care about romance subplots; what makes fans of that stuff swoon just makes me impatient for MORE BLOOD SHRIKING, but even helene's early parts (while by far the best of the three), were more hand-wringing and fact-gathering than wrathbringing. <br><br>eventually it picked up and things got really intense and gripping and the story <i>progressed</i>, but for so long it seemed like everyone was just looking at their watches, killing time. especially elias. seriously, dude, figure your shit out. <br><br>i’m not sure if it’s series fatigue on my part or on the author’s, but the last 1/4 of the book proves there’s still a story to be told and new hearts to break and as always, there’s a strong cliffhanger that makes me eager to see what comes next. i just hope it gets going from the very first inch next time. otherwise, i will be consumed.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1533228360i/26067279._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1532730882204007135" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2245529378" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2245529378" />
    <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson"><img alt="✨    jamieson   ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499961431p2/7706640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2245529378?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780008288754" href="/book/show/37901428-a-reaper-at-the-gates">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=series-to-complete">series-to-complete</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2245529378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16445822321067908448"><i>
  <blockquote>“Curse this world for what it does to the mothers, for what it does to the daughters. Curse it for making us strong through loss and pain, our hearts torn from our chests again and again. Curse it for forcing us to endure.”</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/><b>Look, I'm gonna do something a bit weird here and start with the negatives</b> I REALLY, really enjoyed reading this book but at the same time I had some niggling little issues that I was waiting for some action on and it never came. I need to talk about them. <br/><br/><b>this is an excel</b></span>
  <span id="freeText16445822321067908448" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>“Curse this world for what it does to the mothers, for what it does to the daughters. Curse it for making us strong through loss and pain, our hearts torn from our chests again and again. Curse it for forcing us to endure.”</blockquote>
</i><br><br><b>Look, I'm gonna do something a bit weird here and start with the negatives</b> I REALLY, really enjoyed reading this book but at the same time I had some niggling little issues that I was waiting for some action on and it never came. I need to talk about them. <br><br><b>this is an excellent series in terms of characters</b>. I love the main characters so much. Sabaa Tahir has meticulously worked on her characters individual arcs. The difference between Helene, Elias and especially Laia from the beginning of the series to where it is not is astounding. The best character work is so subtle you don't even notice it's happening <u>and that is what Sabaa Tahir does every. single. time</u> But with that being said, I feel like <i>Sabaa Tahir underused some characters so badly here,</i> and it was extremely disappointing. The climax that A Torch Against the Night ended on, and the anticipation for what she would do with THAT character, was completely killed when that character barely appeared in the book at all. <b>I felt there was so much wasted potential and I was waiting for something that never happened to happen</b>. The lack of payoff and that climax/cliffhanger pretty much going nowhere was so disappointing. A new character who was really interesting was introduced in this book, and I felt not enough was done with him either. On top of that, I really disliked Elias' story arc and where it's going. I just can't get invested in it. But despite my criticisms on character I still really, really loved Laia and Helene's storylines. I really liked the role Laia has stepped into and the political/military heavy nature of Helene's story arc.<br><br><b>My other criticism that I want to get out of the way ties into the above</b> and that is the plot had no clear focus for the first half. The characters current motivations were a little bit unclear, and it felt like characters were just running around the Empire with no goals. The initial focus on making Serric steel was thrown completely out the window midway through. I felt I needed to be more grounded in the plot, especially in the middle section which was a little big wandering. <br><br>That being said, and that is ALL my negatives, the plot overall was really well constructed. The second half especially was explosive and gripping. Sabaa Tahir nails her endings every single time. There was a lot of things HAPPENING with the plot, which was something I really loved. Even though I felt a bit lost at times, I never felt bored, and in a YA fantasy hitting nearly 500 pages thats so important. I found this one way more entertaining than A Torch Against the Night. <br><br><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1535785662i/26233562._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(<a href="https://moonlit-sketches.tumblr.com/post/173982448402/an-ember-in-the-ashes-illustration-from" rel="nofollow noopener">x</a>)</blockquote><br><br><b>One thing I totally loved about this was how much Sabaa Tahir has increased the scope of her world.</b> we're taken to so many new places which I totally loved. I also loved the expansion of the politics with The Mariners and the Warlocks starting to play a larger role in the wars. Whilst the first and second book were quite contained, in this book we follow the characters across the span of the Empire with each view point taking place in a completely different location and I loved that. <br><br>I also loved how the worldbuilding was expanded and more mythology and information around the mythology was added. I loved that the jinn and other magical creatures are starting to play a much, much larger role. <br><br><i>
  <blockquote>“Love. I sigh. Love is joy coupled with misery, elation bound to despair. It is a fire that beckons me gently and then burns when I get too close. I hate love. I yearn for it. And it drives me mad.” </blockquote>
</i><br><br>I continue to really love this series. Even though I had some issues that stopped me rating it 5 stars, I had so much fun reading this. I adore these characters so much. Laia especially is just incredible. She's such a freakin badass but she doesn't have to kickass to be that way. She's just really emotionally strong and persistent and determined and I think it makes her such an excellent heroine to follow. I think Sabaa Tahir does so many things right. The romance is spot on, the characters ares are perfect and the political intrigue is written perfectly. I cannot wait for the next book in the series, I am sure its going to end me.<br><br>tw: marital/spousal abuse, violence, mentions of rape, torture, murder of children</span>
  <a data-text-id="16445822321067908448" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1914444131" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14124275567053086390"><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>Love cannot live here.</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br/><br/>When one of your favorite authors in the world has a new book coming out, it generally becomes your whole world. You have laser focus. Books lose that quality that always seems to drag you in. <b>You obsess and rant and annoy so many people</b>, yet you just could care less-until the day comes and you finally have it in your hands and you can’t devour it quick enough. This is that book. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1520303624ra/25168106.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I just so happened to be one of those lucky Bloggers/Bookstagrammers that was a par</span>
  <span id="freeText14124275567053086390" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>Love cannot live here.</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br><br>When one of your favorite authors in the world has a new book coming out, it generally becomes your whole world. You have laser focus. Books lose that quality that always seems to drag you in. <b>You obsess and rant and annoy so many people</b>, yet you just could care less-until the day comes and you finally have it in your hands and you can’t devour it quick enough. This is that book. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1520303624ra/25168106.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I just so happened to be one of those lucky Bloggers/Bookstagrammers that was a part of the Ember Re-Read tour, and with that came a wonderful perk-I got my beloved Elias book early. That’s right-I finished this book DAYS AGO. Like-before release. It was absolutely wonderful to not worry about spoilers and rabid fangirls (ahem…okay, shut up) ruining any moment of this for me. It was pure solitude and bliss.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote> “It...It hurts.” </blockquote>
</b><br><br>Often when we finally get that book we so crave, it turns out to be a total stinker. Well, I can assure you, this is not the case, here. In fact, I absolutely ADORED IT. <b>It’s been so hard for me lately because I feel as if I’m just so harsh on so many books</b>. I really haven’t connected with too many stories because I just have found SO. MANY. AMAZING. BOOKS this past year that it’s hard for me to be wooed. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>I wonder what he has become in the months we’ve been apart. Has he changed? Is he eating? Taking care of himself? Skies, I hope he has not grown a beard. I <i>hated</i> his beard. </blockquote>
</b><br><br>I can even say that about an all time favorite series, <i>The Red Queen</i>. It just…somewhere along the way, this author lost me. Don’t get me wrong-there was a LOT to love about <i>War Storm</i>. But in <i>King's Cage</i>, when she did some of the things she did….it just didn’t keep my interest. She hurt me in ways I can’t explain-Cal is my DARLING and I just think it was a case of trying to make so many female characters strong, that she almost backpedaled and made some of the more solid moments of the series all for not-just to prove <b>‘I female. I strong.’</b> I get it. We get it. But when a series can stand on it's own two feet, can let the events and the perils and the companionship and mistakes mean something more-now that’s what I come for. These moments can be made into something amazing. Something HUGE. And you’re probably wondering why I’m prattling on about a totally different series-There’s a point, here.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490983013ra/22366289.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Not often am I SO MAD AND LIVID AND ANGRY at an MC…just to forgive them. I don’t do this. I stay mad and angry and livid and what-have-you. But, somehow, <b>Sabaa made Laia someone I adore</b>. I loved her in book one, wanted to stab her [after what she did] in book two, and wanted to hug her in book three. Though, I transferred that hate to another female, but that’s okay. I’m always hating on someone 😉. <br><br>She made a strong, reliable girl that would do anything to save her people. To help them. TO SAVE THOSE GD children [that Sabaa clearly wants to maim and torture repeatedly-Lord help me]-even at the cost of her own life. I don’t know-I really don’t forgive easily. But here? I really did forgive Laia. And the Nightbringer…is it weird I really like him, too, now? Yes, crazy, I know. I’m crazy. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>But even knowing what the Masks would have done, I do not wish to kill. I do not wish to belong to this world of blood and violence and vengeance. I do not wish to be a Mask. </blockquote>
</b><br><br>My point with all that, though, is that even though there is SO MUCH GOING ON and so many characters and so much <i>sadness</i> (I cried so many times-and I rarely cry about books)….<b>Sabaa makes each and every character SHINE</b>. For example? Where my other boy was brought down to an almost sad loser (I still love him, don’t be fooled) by the author’s hand, <b>Sabaa makes Elias an even <i>stronger</i> character</b>-Laia is strong. Elias is strong. Yet-they hurt. They <i>hurt</i>. <i>It hurts</i>. Ugh-you’ll see. <br><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>I’ll go to them as Mask Veturius, dread Martial, soldier of the Empire. I’ll go to them as the estranged, murderous son of the Bitch of Blackcliff, as the monster who killed his friends and assassinated the Empire’s enemies as a child and who watched stonily as Yearlings were whipped to death before his eyes. <br>This time, I will not ask the jinn for help.<br>I will take it. </blockquote>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1529001789ra/25781400.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There wasn’t filler and nothing was unnecessary. OH!!! And I forgot about Helene!! MY GOD THAT GIRL GOES THROUGH SO MUCH IN THIS BOOK. I’m <i>telling</i> you-this book is all pain, I swear. Yet-<b>She remains strong</b>. She doesn’t forget her roots and she does everything in her power to save her people. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote> “Don’t you belittle me. I am the daughter of the Lioness. I destroyed Blackcliff. I saved the life of Elias Veturius. I survived Commandment Keris Veturia. I survived the betrayals of the Resistance <i>and</i> the Nightbringer. I crossed the Empire and broke into Kauf Prison. I rescued my brother and hundreds of other Scholars. I am <i>not</i> nothing.” </blockquote>
</b><br><br>There is literally so much loyalty here. No bashing because someone made a choice-chose a different path-went their own way. These people have sacrificed <i>everything</i>-lost friends. Family. Loved ones. True loves. All for the greater good-all for those they love and can save. All the faults I felt in book two…they faded to ash. Yes, <b>this book was heavy</b>. <i>Yes</i>, there is a LOT of sadness. And <i>yes</i>, I wanted/needed/craved more Elias and Laia moments-but they were there. They were bittersweet, beautiful, and heart-wrenching. <b>Their scenes <i>meant</i> something</b>.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote> “You are cruel, Elias,” she whispers against my mouth. “To give a girl all she desires only to tear it away.” </blockquote>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452789530ra/17743734.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I guess it’s time I say why this series means so much to me-Elias. I mean, is it any surprise, what with all my Elias appreciation posts and whatnot? <b>Never has there been a more selfless hero</b>. No, I’m not kidding. I think the closest thing that comes to mind is Peeta-TOTALLY different guy, situation, scenario, but he’d give it all up just for her. Both of them. Elias could ruin everything in one moment-for the whole world as he knows it-<b>but he can’t give himself up completely</b> if it means Laia will be hurt. <br><br> <b>
  <blockquote>She looks like I feel: broken. I need to let her go. <i>Fight the Nightbringer</i>, I should say. <i>Win. Find joy. Remember me.</i> For why should she come back here? Her future is in the world of the living.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>My heart. I just…CAN’T. He faces so many obstacles in this book I can’t describe or talk about, but just know that heavy is the head that wears the crown-and this applies so many different places. And <b>can we just talk about how bad everything went for EVERYONE in this story</b>? <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>The first time I killed, I was eleven. I saw my enemy’s face for days after he was gone. I heard his voice. And then I killed again. And again. And again. And again. Too soon, I stopped seeing their faces. I stopped wondering what their names were, or who they left behind. I killed because I was ordered to, and then, once free of Blackcliff, I killed because I had to, to stay alive. </blockquote>
</b><br><br>It was one thing after another after another. I could hardly keep up with the pain and destruction. But I have to say-Helene’s, while her storyline has always been a favorite of mine, storyline became a LOT more interesting and, obviously, like everything else in this story, <b>infinitely more heartbreaking</b>. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote> “…One day soon, you will be tested, child. All that you cherish will burn. You will have no friends that day. No allies. No comrades in arms. On that day, your trust in me will be your only weapon.” </blockquote>
</b><br><br><br>My one complaint: The Children. <b>Why the children, Sabaa??</b> I couldn’t reconcile with this in my head. <b>It made me ill</b> and even days later my heart is heavy. It’s fair to say I’m more sensitive because I now have a nugget of my own, but at least two instances in this story hurt me-<b>one broke my soul</b>. I started blubbering to myself and my husband just stared at me like I was crazy. I don’t know if this warrants a lower rating or not, but I think have to deduct half a star because…wwwwWHHHHYYYyyyyy. You authors. You’re so mean lol.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>I know I can die as Soul Catcher. But by the skies, I won’t die by the hand of a ghost-possessed Tribesman choking the life out of me while gibbering in my ear. </blockquote>
</b><br><br>All in all, <b>this book pretty much owns my soul</b>-as does this series and this author (I CANNOT WAIT TO SEE YOU ON THE 20th WOOT!). I bet you’re surprised I didn’t fangirl about my boy more. Well-when all you <i>do</i> is fangirl about said boy for 6 months, you pretty much have room to gush about other things when the time comes. <b>Y’all know he’s my husband</b>. And you also know I would do ANTYHING to get more of him. For once, I’m not angry at an author for prolonging a series. Too often we see authors drag out a series that has no business going past 2/3 books (ahem, see above). But here? I see it. It wasn’t too much. Bad *stuff* had to happen…and here we are. <b>Do I think it will all end okay?</b> For some, yes. I think the world will be fine, in the end. <b>Do I worry for Elias and Laia</b> or just either of them separately, not as a couple? <b>Yes. Yes I do.</b> I don’t know what their end game is-<b>Will Elias be okay? Will LAIA be okay?</b> Who knows. What I <i>do</i>know is that <b>there are many heroic characters to root for here</b>, not just the main two. And that? <u>That’s something to celebrate</u>, all by itself.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1505701447ra/23952137.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But again I imploringly ask: Why all the children, Sabaa? <i>Why??</i> UGHHH.<br><br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a title="Star-Crossed Book Blog" href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1516600667i/24898353._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b> </b>
</u><br><a title="Instagram" href="https://www.instagram.com/starcrossedbookblog/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1516601238i/24898375.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1516601238i/24898372.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="BLOGLOVIN" href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/star-crossed-book-blog-13035961" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><a title="Twitter" href="https://twitter.com/Chels_SCBookblg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468958383i/19764551._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>*****<br><br>How could you, Sabaa<br><br>The tears. They burn. It hurts. It <i>hurts</i> *finger pointy emoji*<br><br>RTC<br><br>***<br><br><b>Brag much?!</b><br><br><a href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/162316188@N08/42676120651/in/dateposted-public/" title="Reaper pics" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528481941i/25689813._SY540_.jpg" width="480" height="640" alt="Reaper pics" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/162316188@N08/42676120841/in/dateposted-public/" title="Reaper pics" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528481941i/25689814._SY540_.jpg" width="480" height="640" alt="Reaper pics" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Did I mention I love Penguin Teen? And that Sabaa and I are besties?.....Didn't think so :P<br><br><br>Dearest Sabaa, <br><br>Let's have a chat, you and I.<br><br>Upon the release of your Elias quote earlier this week for an <i>A Reaper at the Gates</i> preview, it has come to my attention that you intend to cause my main man grief-<b>GOOD</b>. The better for an epic love story.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>"All things have a price, Elias Veturius. The price of saving her will haunt you for all your days. Will you pay it?"</blockquote>
</b><br><br>However. We both know you don't <i>really</i> want to hurt him, now do you? That's what I thought.<br><br><b>We're both rational</b> book [boyfriend] loving gals who could kick it around town whilst singing the praises of all our favorite men and the peril they go through to save their true loves.<br><br>Because that's all it is, right? A story? You'd never <i>actually</i> hurt my baby Elias (my book husband (among many, but this is neither here nor there), thank you)-it's all for the beauty of the story and the theatrics of it all.<br><br>So we'll continue to have these wholly fictional chats over drinks, over nights out on the town, over coffee (or, in my case, Mountain Dew)...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1520526601ra/25182347.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But <b>if you so much as hurt a <i>hair</i> on my Elias's precious little head</b> (more so than you already have), our alliance is severed and I cut all ties to our fictional friendship.<br><br>I'm sorry, but rules are rules, and you can't double cross a friend after you [fictionally] promised to keep a character safe. You can't double cross on the safety of a loved one.<br><br>So-<b>Here's hoping you choose to do the SMART thing</b>. The RATIONAL thing. Don't make me abduct you for ransom. I don't want to have to do this-you don't want me to have to do that, do you? Of course you don't. <b>Do you want me to cry?</b><br><br>Of <i>course</i> not.<br><br>Sincerely,<br><br>Chelsea-Forever your biggest fan<br>AKA Psycho BBF Girl Who Will Go To Drastic Measures To Ensure Her Boys Survive</span>

<div id="review_1689024429" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1689024429" />
    <a title="Beatrice in Bookland" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41218661-beatrice-in-bookland"><img alt="Beatrice in Bookland" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588079280p2/41218661.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1689024429?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beatrice in Bookland" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beatrice in Bookland" href="/user/show/41218661-beatrice-in-bookland">Beatrice in Bookland</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1689024429" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12722444710845014863"><i>"In this fiery hellscape of a world, this mess of blood and madness, justice exists only for those who take it. I'll be damned if I'm not one of them."</i><br/><br/>1) An ember in the ashes ★★★★☆<br/>2) A torch against the night ★★★★★<br/><br/><b>4.5</b><br/><br/>First things first: <b>nothing will ever be as badass as Helene covered in blood fighting with her war hammer</b><br/><br/>Anyway, A reaper at the gates was fantastic. Everything came full circle (even if there's still one book left) and some little things that didn't make sense in the previous ins</span>
  <span id="freeText12722444710845014863" style="display:none"><i>"In this fiery hellscape of a world, this mess of blood and madness, justice exists only for those who take it. I'll be damned if I'm not one of them."</i><br /><br />1) An ember in the ashes ★★★★☆<br />2) A torch against the night ★★★★★<br /><br /><b>4.5</b><br /><br />First things first: <b>nothing will ever be as badass as Helene covered in blood fighting with her war hammer</b><br /><br />Anyway, A reaper at the gates was fantastic. Everything came full circle (even if there's still one book left) and some little things that didn't make sense in the previous instalments were finally explained.<br /><br />Yes, I didn't give it five full stars and that's because imo <b>the first 30-35% of the book is veeery slow and sometimes even hard to follow.</b> Plus, even if I still love him with my whole heart and think that he deserves a future full of rainbows and jam with Laia, <b>I didn't enjoy Elias's storyline.</b><br /><br />But leaving those two things aside, the book is perfect. The first two books were more character driven but this one is <b>very political with a heavy focus on the war.</b> Our three protagonists, Laia, Elias and Helene, are on their own journeys doing different things but they all have the same goal, to protect their loved ones and the world in general.<br /><br />As for <b>the romance,</b> being <i>A reaper at the gates</i> a plot driven book, it's in the background. But when it's there it's painful as hell. I know I shouldn't (because this series will likely end in tears and suffering) but I ship Laia and Elias so much. Every time they're together you can <i>feel</i> the love they have for each other and I hope they're going to get the future of their dreams. And I ship Helene and Harper, too. Their chemistry is off the charts and they both deserve some love in their lives. <s> I ship Helene and her war hammer, too.</s><br /><b>Speaking of Helene,</b> I wasn't the biggest fan of her character in the first two books but in this one she totally won me over. She was my absolute favorite here, no doubts. <br /><br /><b>And goddamn the plot twists.</b> Sabaa Tahir is the queen of the unexpected. We finally get to know, through visions, Laia's mother, who turned out to be another <i>very</i> morally grey character, we find out who Cook is, we get inside the Nightbringer's head and we finally find out what the actual hell Keris (The Commandant) wants and what object is the last piece of the Star (another fucking amazing plot twist and heart wrenching scene).<br /><br />I can't wait to get my hands on the last book, hopefully these three souls will finally get the happiness they deserve.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12722444710845014863" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2227113693" />
    <a title="Beth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44125660-beth"><img alt="Beth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600268807p2/44125660.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth" href="/user/show/44125660-beth">Beth</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780008288754" href="/book/show/37901428-a-reaper-at-the-gates">review of another edition</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44125660-beth?shelf=my-heart-hurts">my-heart-hurts</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2227113693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14113535251399982636">Spoiler Free Review :)<br/><br/><i>”Pain is a choice. Succumb to it and fail. Or defy it and Triumph.”</i><br/><br/>Words cannot express how blissfully <b>happy</b> I am with this. I mean for me it was everything that I could of wanted. I was wondering where the story would go after <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25558608.A_Torch_Against_the_Night__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___2_' title='A Torch Against the Night (An Ember in the Ashes, #2) by Sabaa Tahir' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Torch Against the Night</a> We got updates in what had happened throughout the time on the travels and nothing was left un-said. This time around there’s so much foreboding and it’s setting up the final book perfectly. We see characters grow from stren</span>
  <span id="freeText14113535251399982636" style="display:none">Spoiler Free Review :)<br /><br /><i>”Pain is a choice. Succumb to it and fail. Or defy it and Triumph.”</i><br /><br />Words cannot express how blissfully <b>happy</b> I am with this. I mean for me it was everything that I could of wanted. I was wondering where the story would go after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25558608.A_Torch_Against_the_Night__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___2_" title="A Torch Against the Night (An Ember in the Ashes, #2) by Sabaa Tahir" rel="nofollow noopener">A Torch Against the Night</a> We got updates in what had happened throughout the time on the travels and nothing was left un-said. This time around there’s so much foreboding and it’s setting up the final book perfectly. We see characters grow from strength to strength and take on what they are set up to do, whether we like it or not. Not only this, but we see the cost it brings them, and with this you really see into each characters emotion throughout and <u>that</u> is what I love so much about this book in particular.<br /><br />The build up throughout is nerve wracking, and I honestly got such a strong sense of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33.The_Lord_of_the_Rings__The_Lord_of_the_Rings___1_3_" title="The Lord of the Rings (The Lord of the Rings, #1-3) by J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lord of the Rings</a>and Battle of the Bastards (Game of Thrones) in regards to some of the action… that’s how on edge I was throughout. We’re introduced into new characters (who I love, I can’t deny it, I have a soft spot for Musa) and yet there are so many things left un-said with more questions arising! <br /><br /><i>”Hope is stronger than fear. It is stronger than hate.”</i><br /><br /><u>Characters</u><br /><br />How do I even begin, the love I feel for these characters is on par with those of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18335634.Clockwork_Princess__The_Infernal_Devices___3_" title="Clockwork Princess (The Infernal Devices, #3) by Cassandra Clare" rel="nofollow noopener">Clockwork Princess</a>, and anyone who knows me… knows my love for them! So be prepared for a lot of gushing and me shouting to the rooftops my love for them. That is your warning…<br /><br /><b>Laia</b>. How do I even begin to explain my love for her. I think out of all of the female characters I’ve read Laia is my ultimate queen. I love her relationship with Darin, and it really shows you a strong sense of sibling love. I think the bond they share is just so heartbreaking, she has to deal with a lot in this book, and how she handles it. I literally bow down to her. We see her face her emotions head on and grill I’m proud of her! Her strength and courage gives me <u>everything.</u><br /><br />My heart, <i>Elias.</i> His conundrum in this, my god. My heart literally cannot take it. I can’t cope with it. All he wants to do is protect the people he loves, and just keeps being pulled back to The Waiting Place, my boy needs a break! I need a break. I NEED HIS HAPPINESS! I can’t really say too much because I will end up blabbering everything. But know this, he is too precious for this world and I adore him!<br /><br />You know… when a character you didn’t really like, slowly crawls into your mind and just plants themselves there and once they’re in, you can’t get rid of them, because you realise how much you now actually <u>love</u> them? Oh hello <b>Helene.</b> Her story has gone from strength to strength, and as Blood Shrike she’s just undeniably an amazing character. Once again we see her pushed to her limits. I love her ongoing dispute with Keris and how they’re both playing games with one another trying to best the other. Her loyalty is unfaltering and I just respect this so much! Also… I had such a moment. 3/4 of the way through I realised what is on the cover. It was literally palm to the face moment.<br /><br /><i>The Night Bringer</i> OH MY GOD! I love characters like this, like when there’s someone you can truly dislike, but at the same time kind of link things together. It was so interesting to see him so much, and his plotting my god.<br /><br />Special acknowledgements for; <b>Harper, Musa, Darin and Livia</b>. I know this is a bit of a mix, but I don’t want to go into too much detail with these three! Harper, you know when you don’t know if you should trust them (still I know), his character and his interactions with Helene. Yup. Musa, I need to know more… However I really REALLY liked him. He’s intriguing. Darins representation of PTSD was heartbreaking and it really made you feel for him, but the words he spoke (you know!) broke my poor little heart. Finally Livia, once again I’m surprised by how strong her character became, how she’s as smart as others and her thought process and wit. Well… it’s interesting!<br /><br /><i>”If I seem different, remember that I love you. No matter what happens to me.</i><br /><br />What I <b>liked?</b><br />- I cannot, not mention the names of the chapters, I was literally deceased. That first chapter, then one towards the end. I am not okay. (But SO SO GOOD)<br />- Now… I know this is weird BUT I kind of liked Marcus as a character in this one… now he’s still a little shit don’t get me wrong. But as we know he hears his brother and that side of things is pretty interesting<br />- That bloody tattoo!<br />- All of the ghosts<br />- Seeing Helene “undignified”… <b>howling.</b><br />- Backstory of the Jinn! It messes with you, do I want them to come? Should they stay? STOP MAKING ME FEEL THINGS<br />- Helene vs Keris I love the rivalry, I really do<br />- Visions and back stories my god. MY GOD!<br />- <b>COOK.</b><br />- All of the revenge *evil cackle and rubs hands*<br />- THE NAMES<br />- What we found out, there’s so much and I’m just blown away!<br /><br />What I <b>didn’t like?</b><br />- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7770873.Sabaa_Tahir" title="Sabaa Tahir" rel="nofollow noopener">Sabaa Tahir</a>, you broke my heart on MULTIPLE occasions!<br />- I wish we saw more of certain characters, but that’s only because I was SO invested!<br /><br />Overall I loved this book, it’s setting up Book 4 perfectly, I am on edge, I need to know what happens to all of my characters. I need names, I need answers, I need my bloody ship. The tension is real and I <u>cannot</u> wait.<br /><br /><i>”I’m with you here” He taps my heart”</i><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2201576087?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">An Ember in the Ashes</a> - 5 Stars<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2227107384?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">A Torch Against the Night</a> - 5 Stars<br />A Reaper at the Gates - 5 Stars<br /><br />--------<br />After finishing the book thoughts...<br /><b>I'm not coping.</b><br /><br />1. My heart is broken and has been trampled on.<br />2. It <u>cannot</u> end there, I honestly can't wait however long for the final book, I really can't.<br />3. I need to get my life together after reading this.<br />---------<br /><br />23.12.2019<br /><br />Honestly this book destroyed my soul and yet I love it. That is all.<br />—————<br /><br />21.07.2020<br /><br />I am a crying mess, I honestly think A Sky Beyond the Storm is going to Kill me off. Like I thought Reaper ruined me, but seeing Sabaas updates and just how attached I am to all of the characters.<br /><br />What I find with this is that even thought I absolutely HATE some of these characters I really really enjoy reading about them because they're so interesting. Sometimes when you read about a "Villain" they're not that bad, but The Commandant really is, and as for The Nightbringer I have SO many emotions. <br /><br />I don't know how many times I need to cry about how unfair it is that it seems hopeless that my ship will never ever sail and THEN I have the added heartache of my other ship, Sabaa please give me what I need OR just you know right a nice little chapter for me and I'll be fiiiiiiiiiine!<br /><br />Seriously though, I adore this series but with the way things are going/how it ended it just feels so hopeless and I think whats bothering me is I have literally no idea where this is going to go! I've thought of theories but I'm not really sure if it would actually happen!<br /><br /><b>If you are not up to date I suggest you don't read my theory</b><br /><br />My theory if you're interested is the Helene will become Empress to stand in for her Nephew until he comes of age, I think that Elias AND Laia will both be Soul Catchers but with their Humanity (this is not what I want, I want them to walk off into the sunset holding hands)<br /><br />BUT THEN I also think that one of the big three will die...<br /><br />UNLESS The Commandant and The Nightbringer face the chop?<br /><br />HOWEVER super excited to get Keris's back story! <br /><br />Not a theory but I'm also really really excited to Hel and Laia take the itch of Blackcliff down!<br />--------<br /><br />I need this in my life right now.<br /><br />Also I know we have a cover change... BUT I kind of like it and the meaning behind why it is like it is, my heart!<br /><b>June 12th, come to me ASAP pleaseeee</b><br /><br />No wait... Amazon is telling me 3rd May?!<br />————<br />25.04.18<br />Yep I booked two days off of work just to read this, I need to know what’s going to happen and I have major heart eyes for Elias so it was only common sense really... <br />—————</span>
  <a data-text-id="14113535251399982636" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
